Question: A computer routine was developed to generate two numbers (x,y) the first being a random number between 0 and 100 inclusive, and the second being less than or equal to the square root of the first. Each of the following pair satisfies the routine except
Choices:
  A: (99,10)
  B: (85,9)
  C: (50,7)
  D: (1,1)
  E: (1,0)

  B: x=85, y=9, 9 <= sqrt(85) is true.
  C: x=50, y=7, 7 <= sqrt(50) is true.
  D: x=1, y=1, 1 <= sqrt(1) is true.
  E: x=1, y=0, 0 <= sqrt(1) is true. However, the problem statement specifies that y should be less than or equal to the square root of x. In this case, y is equal to the square root of x. Therefore, E is the pair that does not satisfy the routine.
  The answer is E.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If 75 percent of the employees of a certain company take a winter vacation, 40 percent take a winter and a summer vacation, and 20 percent take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, what Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation?
Choices:
  A: 5%
  B: 15%
  C: 25%
  D: 35%
  E: 45%
Response 0:
Thought:
  We know that 75% of the employees took a winter vacation.
  So, 100% - 75% = 25% of the employees didn't take a winter vacation.
  20% of the employees didn't take either vacation, so 80% of the employees took at least one vacation (winter or summer).
  We know that 40% of the employees took both vacations, so 80% - 40% = 40% of employees took only one vacation (either winter or summer).
  The question is asking us to find the percentage of employees that took a summer vacation but not a winter vacation. Let's call this Q.
  We can use the following formula:  Q = Percentage of employees who took only a summer vacation
                                    = Percentage of employees who took a summer vacation - Percentage of employees who took both vacations
                                    = (100% - 20%) - 40%
                                    = 60% - 40%
  Therefore, Q = 20%.
  The answer is not one of the choices, but the closest one is B: 15%. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are 100 employees in total.
  75% of 100 employees take a winter vacation, so the remaining 25 employees do not take a winter vacation.
  20% of the 100 employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, so 20 employees do not take either vacation.
  Thus, 5 employees take a winter vacation but not a summer vacation (25-20).
  Let x be the number of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  40% of the employees take both winter and summer vacations. If we subtract this from the 75% who take a winter vacation, we get the percentage of employees who take only a winter vacation, which is 35%.
  Therefore, (35 + x + 40 + 20) = 100 [adding all the employees]
  This simplifies to x = 5%
  Thus, 5% of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  The answer is A: 5%
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let's say there are 100 employees in the company.
  75% of the employees take a winter vacation, which is 75 employees.
  40% of the employees take both a winter and a summer vacation, which is 40 employees.
  20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, which is 20 employees.
  Let x be the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  The number of employees who take a summer vacation is the number of employees who take both winter and summer vacations plus the number of employees who take only a summer vacation.
  The number of employees who take only a summer vacation is x% of the number of employees who take a summer vacation, which is (40-x)% of the number of employees who take both winter and summer vacations.
  Therefore,  40-x = 0.6(40) = 24
  Solving gives x = 16.
  Thus, 16% of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  The answer is A: 5%.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought:
  We can use a Venn diagram to solve this problem. Let's consider that:
  - The total number of employees is 100%.
  - 75% of them take a winter vacation.
  - 40% of them take a winter and a summer vacation. Therefore, 40% - 75% = -35% only take a summer vacation.
  - 20% of them take neither a winter nor a summer vacation. Therefore, 20% = -75% + x + -35%, where x is the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  Solving the equation we can get that x = 10%. Therefore, 10% of employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.

Thought:
Let's say there are 100 employees in the company.
75% of the employees take a winter vacation which is 75 employees
40% of the employees take a winter and a summer vacation which is 40 employees
20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation which is 20 employees
We need to find out the percentage of employees who take summer vacation but not the winter vacation.
Let's represent the percentage of employees who take summer vacation but not winter as Q.
100 = 75 + Q + 20 (the sum of three sets of employees, those taking summer but not winter, taking winter and summer, and taking neither must equal 100)
Q = 5%
Therefore, 5% of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.

Response 5:
Thought:
  We can use a Venn diagram to solve the problem.
  Let W be the set of employees who take a winter vacation.
  Let S be the set of employees who take a summer vacation.
  Then 75% of the employees are in WUC (U is union, C is complement).
  40% of the employees are in W∩S.
  20% of the employees are outside (W∪S)C.
  We want to find Q (% of employees in S\W).
  We can use the formula for three sets: n(W∪S∪C) = n(W) + n(S) + n(C) - n(W∩S) - n(W∩C) - n(S∩C) + n(W∩S∩C),
  where n(X) is the number of employees in the set X.
  Plugging in the numbers, we get:
  100% = 75% + Q + 5% - 40% - n(W∩C) - n(S∩C) + 20%,
  Simplifying, we get:
  100% = 60% + Q - n(W∩C) - n(S∩C).
  We know that n(W∩C) = 0 and n(S∩C) = 20%, so
  Q = 100% - 60% - 20% = 20%.
  Therefore, 20% of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.

Response 6:
Thought:
Let n be the total number of employees of the company.
Then, the number of people who take only a winter vacation is 75% - 40% = 35% of n.
Let x be the percentage of people taking only a summer vacation.
Then, n * 0.2 people take no vacation.
The percentage of people who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is x - 40% of x, which is the percentage of employees who take both a summer and a winter vacation.
We can now create an equation from the given information:
n * 0.2 = 100 - 75 - 35 - x + 40x
This simplifies to:
n * 0.2 = -40x - 10
We can simplify this again to:
2n = -200x - 50
From this equation, we see that x = (2n + 50)/(-200)
So the percentage of the employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is x - 40% of x:
x - 40% of x = x - 0.4x = 0.6x
Substituting the value of x we found above, we get:
0.6[(2n + 50)/(-200)] = -(n + 25)/(666.67)
Therefore, Q is approximately -15%.

  Let W be the set of employees that take a winter vacation.
  Let S be the set of employees that take a summer vacation.
  By the principle of inclusion-exclusion, we have |W ∪ S| = |W| + |S| - |W ∩ S|.
  We are given that |W| = 75%|E|, |W ∩ S| = 40%|E|, and |¬(W ∪ S)| = 20%|E|.
  We want to find |S \ W|.
  |W ∪ S| = |E \ ¬(W ∪ S)| = (100% - 20%)|E| = 80%|E|.
  Therefore, 80%|E| = 75%|E| + |S| - 40%|E|.
  Solving for |S \ W|, we get |S \ W| = 15%|E|.
  Therefore, the answer is Q = 15%.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 3 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular solid, 3 x 4 x 15, is inscribed in a sphere, so that all eight of its vertices are on the sphere. What is the diameter of the sphere?
Choices:
  A:  13.3542
  B:  15.8113
  C:  18.3451
  D:  19.5667
  E:  20.8888
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The longest diagonal of a rectangular solid is also the diameter of the sphere.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid, which is also the diameter of the sphere, can be found using the Pythagorean Theorem.
  The Pythagorean Theorem states that for a right triangle with side lengths a, b, and c (where c is the hypotenuse), a^2 + b^2 = c^2.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is the square root of (3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2), which simplifies to the square root of 250.
  The diameter of the sphere is twice the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid.
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is 2*sqrt(250), which simplifies to 2*5*sqrt(10), which is 10sqrt(10).
  The answer is none of the listed choices.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  A rectangular solid with dimensions 3 x 4 x 15 has a longest diagonal of length sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250).
  If this diagonal is the diameter of the sphere, then the radius of the sphere is 1/2 * sqrt(250).
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is sqrt(250) and the answer is A: 13.3542.

d1 = sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) ≈ 15.2315
d2 = sqrt(3^2 + 15^2 + 4^2) ≈ 15.2315
d3 = sqrt(4^2 + 15^2 + 3^2) ≈ 15.2315
d4 = sqrt(15^2 + 4^2 + 3^2) ≈ 15.2315

The longest diagonal is d1, which gives us the diameter of the sphere.
Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is ≈ 15.2315 x 2, ≈ 30.463

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Peter wants to find 10 additional people to form a scavenger hunt team with him. If he has 10 friends who would like to participate, how many choices does he have for forming his team?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 1
  C: 2
  D: 3
  E: 4
Response 0:
Thought:
  Peter wants to find 10 additional people to form a scavenger hunt team with him.
  He has 10 friends who would like to participate.
  No friend can be on the team more than once.
  The number of ways to choose 10 people from 10 friends is 10 choose 10 which is equal to 1.
  Therefore, he has 1 choice for forming his team.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  There are 10 people to choose from.
  Peter wants to choose 10 people to form his team.
  The order does not matter since it is just a group of people.
  This is a combination problem since order doesn't matter.
  The number of ways to choose a combination of r objects from a set of n objects is given by nCr, which is equal to n! / r!(n - r)!.
  In this problem, n = 10 and r = 10.
  So, the number of ways to choose 10 people out of 10 is 10! / 10! * (10-10)! which is equal to 1.
  Therefore, Peter has only 1 choice for forming his team.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Peter wants to choose 10 people from his 10 friends to join the scavenger hunt team.
  If he has 10 friends and he wants to choose 10 of them, there is only one way to form his team since he has to choose all of them.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 1.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  Peter wants to form a team of 10 people in addition to himself.
  He has 10 friends who would like to participate.
  The number of people he can select from is 10.
  Since Peter wants to select 10 people for his team, we will be choosing 10 people from 10 people.
  The formula for choosing r items from n items (order doesn't matter) is given as n choose r (written as C(n,r)) which is equivalent to n!/[r!*(n-r)!].
  Plugging in the values, we get 10 choose 10 which is equal to 10!/[10!*(10-10)!] which simplifies to 1.
  Therefore, Peter has only one choice for forming his team.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 4:
Thought:
  Peter wants to add 10 more people to his scavenger hunt team.
  He already has 10 friends to participate with him.
  The order of selection doesn't matter, since it is a team.
  He needs to choose 10 people from 10+10=20 people in total.
  The number of ways to do this is 20 choose 10.
  We can use the formula n choose k = n! / (k! * (n-k)!) to find this.
  Therefore, the answer is 20! / (10! * (20-10)!) = 184,756.

  Peter wants to form a scavenger hunt team with 10 people.
  He already has 10 friends who would like to participate.
  The number of choices for forming his team is the number of ways to select the remaining 10 people from the 10 available friends.
  This can be calculated using combination.
  We can use the formula C( n, r) = n! / (r! * (n-r)!), where n is the total number of people and r is the number of people we want to choose.
  In this case, n = 10 and r = 10.
  So, C(10, 10) = 10! / (10! * 0!) = 1.
  Therefore, Peter has only one choice for forming his team.

  Peter wants to add 10 additional people to his team.
  He has 10 friends who want to participate.
  To find the number of choices Peter has, we need to find the number of ways he can choose 10 people from the 10 friends who want to participate.
  This is a combination problem where we need to choose 10 people from a set of 10 people.
  The formula for a combination is n choose k = n! / (k! * (n-k)!).
  In this case, n = 10 and k = 10 because we need to choose all 10 people from the set of 10 friends.
  Plugging in the values, we get 10 choose 10 = 10! / (10! * (10-10)!) = 1.
  Therefore, Peter has only 1 choice for forming his team.

  nCr = n! / (r!*(n-r)!), where n = total number of people that Peter can form a team with (10+10=20)
  and r = number of people Peter needs to choose to form a team (10).
  So the number of choices Peter has for forming his team is 20C10, which can be calculated as:
  20C10 = 20! / (10!*(20-10)!) = 184,756.
  Therefore, Peter has 184,756 choices to form his team.

Question: An express electric train takes exact three seconds to enter tunnel which is 1 mile long.
If train is traveling at 120 mile an hour, how long will it take to pass completely through the tunnel ?
Choices:
  A: 43 seconds
  B: 39 seconds
  C: 20 seconds
  D: 33 seconds
  E: 55 seconds
Response 0:

- We can convert the speed of the train from miles per hour to feet per second by multiplying by 5280/3600
- The train enters the tunnel in 3 seconds
- We can use the formula distance = speed * time to calculate the distance of the train when it completely passes through the tunnel
- The distance of the train when it completely passes through the tunnel is 1 mile + the length of the train
- We can convert the distance to feet 
- We solve for time using distance = speed * time
- We need to add the 3 seconds for the train to enter the tunnel
- Therefore, the total time is the time it takes the train to pass completely through the tunnel plus the 3 seconds it takes to enter it.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
- To enter the tunnel, the train takes 3 seconds.
- The tunnel is 1 mile long.
- The speed of the train is 120 miles per hour.
- The time it will take to pass completely through the tunnel will depend on the total distance covered by the train and the tunnel.
- The total distance the train needs to cover to pass through the tunnel is 2 miles (1 mile to enter the tunnel + 1 mile to exit the tunnel).
- To determine the time, we can use the formula: time = distance / speed.

Calculation:
- Total distance = 2 miles
- Speed of train = 120 miles per hour
- Time = Distance / Speed
- Time = 2 miles / 120 miles per hour
- Time = 1/60 hours
- Time = (1/60) x 60 minutes
- Time = 1 minute

Conversion:
- 1 minute = 60 seconds

Therefore, the answer is D: 33 seconds.

Question: A bookshelf contains 45 books, 30 of which are hardcover and 20 of which are fiction. What is the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 15
  C: 18
  D: 20

Response 0:
Thought: 
  We know that there are 45 books total, 30 of which are hardcover and 20 of which are fiction. 
  Let x be the number of books that are both hardcover and fiction. 
  To find the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction, we need to find the smallest possible number of hardcover books or fiction books, and take the smaller of these two numbers.
  The maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction is therefore equal to the minimum of the number of hardcover books and the number of fiction books.
  The number of hardcover books that are not fiction is 30 - x.
  The number of fiction books that are not hardcover is 20 - x.
  The maximum value of x is therefore min(30 - x, 20 - x).
  To find this value, we can set the two expressions equal to each other and solve for x:
  30 - x = 20 - x
  x = 10
  Therefore, the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction is 10.

  Therefore, (Height of Pole / Length of Shadow of Pole) = (Height of Tree / Length of Shadow of Tree)
  14 / 10 = 
  x / 15
  Solve for x
  x = (14 / 10) * 15
  x = 21
  The height of the tree is 21 meters
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume the height of the tree is h.
  The electric pole is 14 meters high.
  The shadow cast by the electric pole is 10 metres.
  The shadow of the tree is 15 meters.
  According to the concept of similar triangles, the ratios of the corresponding sides of two similar triangles are equal.
  Therefore, the ratio of the height of the pole to its shadow is equal to the ratio of the height of the tree to its shadow.
  From this, we can write an equation as follows: `h / 15 = 14 / 10`
  Solving for h: `h = (15 * 14) / 10 = 21`
  Therefore, the height of the tree is 21 meters.
Action: Answer("A")

  That is, 
  14 : x = 10 : 15
  Cross-multiplication gives
  10x = 14 x 15
  x = (14 x 15)/10
  x = 21
  Therefore, the height of the tree is 21 meters.

Question: At what price should the Karan mark a sewing machine that costs him Rs. 1200/- so that even after offering a 20% discount, he makes 20% profit?
Choices:
  A: 1,879
  B: 1,875
  C: 1,876
  D: 1,872
  E: 1,800
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's say the selling price is x.
  The cost price of the sewing machine is Rs. 1200.
  Therefore, the profit percentage is 20%.
  That means the selling price is 120% of the cost price.
  (120/100)*1200 = 1440 is the selling price he should set to earn a 20% profit.
  Now he is offering a 20% discount which means he will sell the item at 80% of the selling price.
  Selling price with discount = (80/100)*1440 = 1152
  Therefore, the price Karan should mark on the sewing machine is Rs. 1875.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
To calculate the selling price of the sewing machine, we need to add the profit to the cost price.
If the cost price is Rs. 1200 and Karan wants to make a 20% profit, then his selling price would be:
Selling price = Cost price + Profit
Profit = 1200 x 20/100 = Rs. 240/-
Selling price = Cost price + Profit = Rs. 1200 + Rs. 240 = Rs. 1440/-
If Karan wants to offer a 20% discount on the selling price, then his selling price would be:
Discount = 20%
Selling price - Discount = 80% of Selling price
80% of Selling price = Rs. 1440
Selling price = Rs. 1440 / 80 x 100 = Rs. 1800
Therefore, Karan should sell the sewing machine for Rs. 1800

Question: John would make the 3-letter codes with diffenrent 5 vowels and 20 consonants with the condition that the middle letter must be vowel and the first letter and the third letter must be different from each other and are both consonant. How many different codes can be made?
Choices:
  A: 1,980
  B: 2,020
  C: 2,100
  D: 2,200
  E: 1,900
Response 0:
Thought:
  There are 5 choices for the middle letter which must be a vowel.
  There are 20 choices for the first letter which must be a consonant.
  There are 19 choices remaining for the third letter which must be a different consonant from the first letter.
  Therefore, there are 20*19=380 ways to choose the first and the third letters.
  The number of possible 3-letter codes is the product of the number of choices for each letter, which is 5*380*5.
  Therefore, the answer is 9,500.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  There are 5 choices for the middle letter, which must be a vowel.
  There are 20 choices for the first and third letters, which must be different from each other and are both consonant.
  There are 19 remaining consonants to choose from for the third letter because we can't choose the letter we used for the first letter.
  The number of different codes that can be made is the product of the number of choices for each position.
  Therefore, the answer is 5 x 20 x 19 = 1,900.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Out of 5 vowels, 1 vowel can be selected in 5C1 ways.
  Out of 20 consonants, 2 consonants can be selected in 20C2 ways.
  The 2-selected consonants can be arranged in 2! ways and the selected vowel can be placed in 1 way.
  Therefore, the total number of codes can be made as (5C1) × (20C2) × 2! × 1 = 1,980.
  The answer is A: 1,980.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 11 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: At a certain factory, 10 percent of the staplers produced on Monday were defective and 2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. If 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, what was the number of staplers produced that day?
Choices:
  A: 4,000
  B: 4,200
  C: 4,500
  D: 4,800
  E: 5,000
Response 0:
Thought: 
Let x be the number of staplers produced that day.
10% of x staplers were defective, so 0.1x staplers were defective.
Therefore, (0.9x) is the number of non-defective staplers produced that day.
2% of the non-defective staplers were rejected, which means (0.02)(0.9x) = 72.
Simplifying that equation, we get 0.018x = 72
Solving for x, we have x = 4000.
Therefore, the number of staplers produced that day is 4,000.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's assume that the factory has produced x number of staplers.
On Monday, 10% of x staplers produced were defective.
Therefore, there were (x*10/100) defective staplers.
Non-defective staplers = x - (x*10/100) = (9/10)*x
2% of the non-defective ones were rejected, which were 72, 
So, (2/100) * (9/10) * x = 72
Solving the equation, we get x = 4,000
Therefore, the number of staplers produced on Monday was 4,000.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 12 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: M men agree to purchase a gift for Rs. D. If 3 men drop out how much more will each have to contribute towards the purchase of the gift?
Choices:
  A: D/(M-3)
  B: MD/3
  C: M/(D-3)
  D: 3D/(M2-3M)
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Initially, each person would have to contribute D/M amount of money for the gift.
  If 3 men drop out, then M-3 men will be purchasing the gift.
  Therefore, each person will have to contribute D/(M-3) amount of money for the gift.
  The difference between the amount each person had to contribute initially and now would be:
  D/M - D/(M-3) = 3D/(M*(M-3))
  Therefore, each person will have to contribute 3D/(M*(M-3)) more towards the purchase of the gift.
  The answer is D: 3D/(M2-3M)
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Initially, M men agreed to purchase a gift for Rs. D.
  The contribution of each man is D/M.
  When 3 men dropped out, M-3 men have to bear the expense of the gift.
  So, the new contribution of each man is D/(M-3).
  The difference between the new and old contributions of each man is [(D/(M-3)) - (D/M)].
  After simplification, the expression becomes D/(M(M-3)).
  Therefore, each man has to contribute D/(M(M-3)) more when 3 men drop out.
  The answer is D: 3D/(M2-3M).
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:

  When 3 men dropped out, there were (M-3) men left to contribute towards the gift.

  Therefore, the new contribution amount per person would be D/(M-3).
  The difference in contribution amount would be the old contribution amount minus the new contribution amount.
  That would be D/M - D/(M-3) = 3D/(M(M-3)).
  Therefore, the answer is D: 3D/(M2-3M).

  If 3 men drop out, the total number of men who will contribute towards the purchase of the gift will be (M-3).

  The new contribution can be calculated as (D/(M-3)) + x, where x is the additional amount that each man contributes.
  We know that the total contribution of the remaining men towards the gift should be the same as the initial contribution of all the men.
  Therefore, we can write the equation as: D/M = [(D/(M-3)) + x]/(M-3)
  Solving for x, we get: x = D/((M-3)*3)
  Therefore, each man will have to contribute an additional amount of D/((M-3)*3) towards the purchase of the gift.
  The answer is D: 3D/(M2-3M).
Action: Answer("D")

  In this case, we have ties of 5 different colors.
  The worst-case scenario is when we take out one tie of each color, which would give us a total of 5 ties.

Question: The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs?
Choices:
  A: 0.5
  B: 0.6
  C: 0.7
  D: 0.8
  E: 0.9
Response 0:
Thought:
  P(A) = 0.6, so P(A') = 0.4
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  Since A and B are independent, P(A and B) = P(A)P(B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) -  0.6P(B)
  Solving for P(B), we get P(B) = 0.8
  Therefore, the answer is D: 0.8.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let P(A) be the probability that event A occurs and P(B) be the probability that event B occurs.
  Using the formula for the probability of the union of two events, P(A U B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A ∩ B), where P(A ∩ B) is the probability that both A and B occur, we have:
  P(A U B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A)P(B), since A and B are independent.
  We know P(A) = 0.6, and P(A U B) = 0.96.
  Substituting these values into the equation above, we get:
  0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.6P(B)
  Solving for P(B), we get:
  P(B) = (0.96 - 0.6) / (1 - 0.6) = 0.6
  Therefore, the probability that event B occurs is 0.6.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let A and B be two events such that A and B are independent.
  Probability of A = P(A) = 0.6
  Probability of at least one of A or B = P(A U B) = 0.96
  Using the formula P(A U B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A ∩ B), we can find P(B).
  We know P(A) and P(A U B), so let's solve for P(B).
  P(A U B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A ∩ B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - P(A ∩ B)
  Since A and B are independent, P(A ∩ B) = P(A) × P(B) = 0.6 × P(B).
  0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.6 × P(B)
  0.36 = 0.4 × P(B)
  P(B) = 0.36 / 0.4 = 0.9
  Therefore, the probability that event B occurs is 0.9.
  The answer is E: 0.9.

Question: The price of a product is reduced by 30% . By what percentage should it be increased to make it 100%
Choices:
  A: 41.86%
  B: 42.86%
  C: 43.86%
  D: 44.86%
  E: 45.86%
Response 0:
Thought:
  If the price of a product is reduced by 30%, then the selling price becomes 70% of the original price. 
  If we need to increase the selling price back to the original price, we need to increase it by a factor that is equal to 100/70. 
  Therefore, we need to increase it by (100/70 - 1) * 100%, which simplifies to approximately 42.86%. 
  The answer is B: 42.86%.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let the original price of the product be  "x".
  A 30% reduction means the new price of the product is  (x - 0.3x) = 0.7x.
  To find the percentage increase required to make it 100%, we need to find the percentage increase from 0.7x to x:
  Percentage increase = (change in price/ original price) * 100 %
                      = [(x - 0.7x)/0.7x] * 100 %
                      = (0.3x/0.7x) * 100 %
                      = (3/7) * 100%
                      = 42.86%
  Therefore, the answer is B: 42.86%

Topic: Math
Question: A flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. The height of building, which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions will be :
Choices:
  A: 12 metre
  B: 12.5 metre
  C: 13.5 metre
  D: 14 metre
  E: 15 metre
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can solve this problem using the concept of similar triangles.
  Let the height of the building be x metre.
  Then, we have the following proportion of similar triangles:
        height of flagstaff / length of shadow of flagstaff = height of building / length of shadow of building
        17.5 / 40.25 = x / 28.75
  Solving for x, we get:
        x = 17.5 * 28.75 / 40.25
        x = 12.5
  Therefore, the height of the building is 12.5 metre.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We can use the concept of similar triangles to solve this problem.
  The ratio of the length of the flagstaff to its shadow is the same as the ratio of the height of the building to its shadow.
  Therefore, we can set up the proportion: 
  height of building / length of its shadow = height of flagstaff / length of its shadow
  Then solve for the height of the building.
  height of building = (length of its shadow * height of flagstaff) / length of the flagstaff's shadow
  
Calculation: 
  height of building = (28.75 * 17.5) / 40.25 = 12.5
  
Answer: Answer("B")  (12.5 metre)
Response 2:
Thought:

  Therefore, h/28.75 = 17.5/40.25

  Therefore, the height of building is 12.5 meters.
  The answer is B: 12.5 meter.

Question: Suppose you want to arrange your English, Hindi, Mathematics, History, Geography and Science books on a shelf. In how many ways can you do it ?
Choices:
  A: 520
  B: 720
  C: 920
  D: None
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Thought:
  The number of ways to arrange books is equal to the number of permutations.
  There are 6 books to arrange, so we need to find the permutation of 6 books.
  The formula for permutation of n objects is n!
  Therefore, the number of ways to arrange 6 books is  6! = 720.
  The answer is B: 720.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The question is asking us to find the number of permutations of 6 books. 
  We can use the formula for permutations of n objects taken r at a time: P(n, r) = n!/(n-r)!.
  In this case, we want to arrange all 6 books, so r = 6.
  Therefore, the number of ways to arrange the books is P(6,6) = 6!/(6-6)! = 6! = 720.
  The answer is B: 720.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 20 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers?
Choices:
  A: (zy – 2x)/z
  B: (zy – 2)/z
  C: (zx – y)/(z – 2)
  D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2)
  E: (zy – x)/(z + 2)
Response 0:
Thought:
  The average of the highest and lowest score = x.
  The sum of the highest and lowest score = 2x.
  The average score for the entire class = y.
  The sum of all scores in the class = y * z.
  Let's assume that the highest and lowest scores are not included.
  There are z-2 students left to average, whose sum is (y * z) - (highest score) - (lowest score).
  The average of these students is ((y * z) - 2x) / (z - 2).
  Therefore, the answer is (zy – 2x)/(z -2).
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let L be the lowest score and H be the highest score in the class.
  We know: (L + H)/2 = x      ---(1)
           (sum of all scores in the class) / z = y   ---(2)
  Let A be the average of the class, excluding the highest and the lowest score.
  We know: A = (sum of all scores - L - H) / (z - 2)  ---(3)
  Now, the sum of all the scores can be written as z times the average score, which is y. So, we can say:
             (sum of all scores) = z * y
  Therefore, (sum of all scores - L - H) = (z * y) - L - H
  Substituting this and equation (1) in equation (3) and simplifying, we get
             A = (zy - 2x)/(z - 2)
  Therefore, the answer is D: (zy - 2x)/(z - 2).
Action: Answer("D")

  There are z - 2 students whose score contributed to the sum of all scores excluding the highest and the lowest scores.
  Therefore, the average score of the class excluding the highest and lowest scores = (zy - 2x)/(z-2).

Question: Silu and Meenu were walking on the road.

  A: 12
  B: 28
  C: 27
  D: 58
  E: 91

Now we can solve for X to find Meenu's weight.
Subtracting X from both sides we get X = 58, which means Meenu weighs 58 Kgs.
Therefore, the answer is D: 58.

  B: 60%
  C: 70%
  D: 86%
  E: 90%
Response 0:

  The astronaut weighs 211 pounds on Earth and weighs 182 pounds on Venus.
  The weight of the astronaut on Venus as a percentage of the astronaut's weight on Earth is: (182/211) x 100 ≈ 86%
  Therefore, the answer is D: 86%.

  Therefore, the answer is D: 86%.

Question: At its maximum speed, a space shuttle can travel 700m high in 40 seconds. It will also take 5 seconds to pass a point. What then is the length of the space shuttle?
Choices:
  A: 50 m
  B: 75 m
  C: 100 m
  D: 125 m
  E: 150 m
Response 0:
Thought: 
  If the space shuttle reaches a height of 700 meters in 40 seconds, then we can find its speed by dividing the distance by the time: 700 m ÷ 40 s = 17.5 m/s
  The length of the space shuttle is its speed multiplied by the time it takes to pass a point: 17.5 m/s × 5 s = 87.5 meters
  Therefore, the length of the space shuttle is 87.5 meters.
Action: Answer("None of the Above") # The answer is not among the choices. The correct answer is 87.5 meters.
Response 1:
Thought:

  We are given it will take 5 seconds to pass a point, which we can assume to be the length of the shuttle.
  So, the length of the shuttle is the distance traveled in 5 seconds.
  To calculate that, we can use the formula: 
  distance = speed x time
  The speed of the shuttle can be found using the distance traveled in 40 seconds.
  speed = distance/time = 700m/40s = 17.5m/s
  Therefore, distance traveled in 5 seconds = speed x time = 17.5m/s x 5s = 87.5m
  So, the length of the space shuttle is 87.5 meters.
  The answer is E: 150 m.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 24 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. If the yard has an area of 240 square meters, how many meters of fencing does she need?
Choices:
  A: 58
  B: 62
  C: 66
  D: 70
  E: 74
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Alice wants to fence three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side unfenced, which means she needs fencing for three sides.
  Let's assume that the sides of the rectangular yard are 'l' and 'w'. 
  Since the area of the yard is 240 square meters, we know that l*w = 240. 
  We also know that one of the sides (width) is 10 meters less than one of the sides that needs fencing. 
  We can write an equation for the total amount of fencing needed: 2l + w = (2l + (w + 10)) + w + (2l + (w + 10))
  Simplifying gives 4l + 2w = 2w + 50 + 2l, which reduces to 2l = 25.
  Substituting the value of 2l (i.e. 25) into the equation for total amount of fencing gives 2l + 2w + 10 = 2(25) + 2w + 10 = 60.
  Therefore, Alice needs 60 meters of fencing.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
   If Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced, then the perimeter of the rectangular yard will be:
   p=2L+10+W
   where L and W are the length and width of the rectangular yard respectively.
   
   The area of the rectangular yard is given by:
   A=L.W=240
   
   We can solve for L in terms of W from the equation for area:
   L = 240 / W
   
   We can substitute this expression for L in the equation for the perimeter:
   p = 2L + 10 + W = 2(240/W) + 10 + W
   
   To minimize the amount of fencing required, we need to find the value of W that minimizes the perimeter.
   To do that, we can find the value of W that makes the derivative of p with respect to W equal to zero:
   
   dp/dW = -480 / W^2 + 1
   
   Setting dp/dW = 0, we get:
   
   -480 / W^2 + 1 = 0
   W = sqrt(480) = 4*sqrt(30)
   
   Substituting this value of W back into the equation for p, we get:
   
   p = 2L + 10 + W = 2(240/W) + 10 + W = 60/sqrt(30) + 10 + 4*sqrt(30) = 20*sqrt(30) + 10
   
   Rounding to the nearest whole number, we get p = 62 meters.
   
   Therefore, Alice needs 62 meters of fencing.
   
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
Area of a rectangular yard is length x width.
Let's suppose that the length of the yard is x and the width of the yard is y.
If the area of the yard is 240 square meters, then xy = 240.
Since the fencing is required for three sides, the perimeter of the yard is calculated as follows:
Perimeter of the yard = x + y + x = 2x + y.
If one side is left unfenced and the length of the unfenced side is 10 meters, then the perimeter of the yard will be equal to: 
2x + y - 10.
The equation for the perimeter of the yard is: 2x + y - 10 = P, where P is the perimeter.
We need to calculate P.
Since xy = 240, we can solve for y, which is y = 240/x. 
Substitute y with 240/x in 2x + y - 10 = P, we get 2x + (240/x) - 10 = P.
It can be simplified to the quadratic equation:
2x^2 - 10x + 240 = Px
By solving for x, we get x = 12 and x = 10.
Since we need to fence only three sides, we will consider the value of x as 12, which gives us a larger perimeter.
Plugging in the value of x = 12, we can find the value of y = 20.
Therefore, the perimeter of the yard is 2x + y - 10 = 34 + 20 - 10 = 44 meters.
The answer is D: 70.

  Since the rectangular yard has three fenced sides, we can represent its perimeter as P = 2L + x, where L is the length of the yard.

  We also know that one side of 10 meters is unfenced. This means that the perimeter of the fenced portion of the yard is P - 10.

    -480 / x^2 + 1 = 0
    x^2 = 480

    Fenced perimeter ≈ 2 * (240 / 21.91) + 21.91 - 10 ≈ 62.1

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 25 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A sporting goods store carries only yellow and white golf balls. At the beginning of the day it had 600 golf balls in stock, and by the end of the day it had sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls. If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, and in doing so sold all of its white golf balls, how many yellow golf balls did the store have to begin the day?
Choices:
  A: 80
  B: 120
  C: 240
  D: 320
  E: 360
Response 0:
Thought:
At the beginning of the day, the store had 600 golf balls in total.
By the end of the day, 80% of the inventory was sold, so the store sold 0.8 * 600 = 480 golf balls
Since the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, then 50% of the total number of golf balls were white.
If all the white golf balls got sold, then the remaining 50% of the golf balls were yellow.
So, the store had 0.5 * 600 = 300 yellow golf balls in stock at the beginning of the day.
The answer is E: 360.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The store sold 80% of its golf balls by the end of the day, so 20% of the golf balls are remaining.
  The remaining 20% is equivalent to 120 golf balls (since 80% was sold, which is equivalent to 80% of 600 = 480, then the remaining 20% will be 120).
  Since the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, the number of white golf balls they sold is equal to the number of yellow golf balls sold.
  Therefore, the store had 60 white golf balls and 60 yellow golf balls to begin with.
  This is a total of 120 golf balls to begin with, so the answer is B: 120.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
At the beginning of the day, the store had 600 golf balls in stock.
By the end of the day, they sold 80% of the inventory, which is 0.8 x 600 = 480 golf balls.
Let x be the number of yellow golf balls in stock at the beginning of the day.
Since the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, then the beginning inventory of white golf balls must also be x.
Therefore, the total number of golf balls sold is 480 = (x + x) = 2x.
Solving for x, we get x = 240.
Therefore, the store had 240 yellow golf balls at the beginning of the day.
The answer is C: 240.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 26 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The bus fare for two persons for travelling between Agra and Aligarh id four-thirds the train fare between the same places for one person. The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512. Find the train fare between the two places for one person?
Choices:
  A: 126
  B: 77
  C: 88
  D: 66
  E: 54
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let 'x' be the train fare for one person. 
  Then, the bus fare for two persons is (4/3)x
  The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus is 6(4/3)x = 8x. 
  Also, the total fare paid by 8 persons travelling by train is 8x. 
  The total fare paid by both groups is Rs. 1512. 
  Therefore, 8x + 8x = 1512, which gives 16x = 1512 and x = 94.5.
  Hence, the train fare between the two places for one person is Rs. 94.5
  The answer is none of the above.
  
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's assume that train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person is x. 
According to the question, bus fare for two persons between Agra and Aligarh is (4/3)x. Therefore, bus fare for one person is (2/3)x. 
The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512. 
So, (6 * (2/3)x) + (8 * x) = 1512
Simplifying the above equation, we get x = 84.
Therefore, the train fare between the two places for one person is Rs. 84.
Action: Answer("None of the above”) - The correct answer is not in the given choices.
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let the train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person be x.
  The bus fare for two persons is four-thirds of the train fare for one person. Therefore, the bus fare for two persons is (4/3)x.
  Let the train fare for 8 persons be y. Therefore, the train fare for one person is y/8.
  Let the bus fare for 6 persons be z. Therefore, the bus fare for two persons is z/3.
  According to the problem, the total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512.
  Therefore, 6(z/3) + 8(y/8) = 1512
  2z + y = 504 * 3
  2(4/3)x + y = 1512
  (8/3)x + y = 1512
  (8/3)x + 2z = 504 * 3
  (8/3)x + 2(4/3) x = 1512
  (8/3)x + (8/3)x = 1512 - 8 * 4/3
  (16/3)x = 1504
  x = (1504 * 3) / 16
  x = 282
  Therefore, the train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person is Rs.282.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 27 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Jim filled his dog's bowl with dog food. Starting at 8:00 am, Jim's dog ate exactly once an hour, consuming exactly 1/3 of the dog food remaining in the bowl at each feeding session. Approximately, what percent of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon of the same day?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 25%
  C: 30%
  D: 35%
  E: 40%
Response 0:
Thought:
  The dog ate at 8:00 am, 9:00 am, 10:00 am, and 11:00 am, so four times in total.
  At each feeding, the dog consumed 1/3 of the food remaining in the bowl, so the amount of food remaining in the bowl would be 2/3 of the amount from the previous hour.
  Therefore, the amount of food remaining in the bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon would be equal to: 1 (the original amount) times 2/3 times 2/3 times 2/3 times 2/3, which is equal to approximately 0.2 (rounded to the nearest hundredth).
  So, approximately 20% of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The dog ate every hour starting from 8:00am until noon, which is 4 hours.
  The dog ate 1/3 of the remaining food in the bowl at each feeding session
  Since the dog ate once at each of the 4 hour, there were 4 feeding sessions.
  Let's assume there were originally 100 units of dog food in the bowl (to make it easier to calculate percentages).
  The first session, the dog ate 1/3 of 100, leaving 2/3 of 100 which is 66.67
  The second session, the dog ate 1/3 of 66.67, leaving 2/3 of 66.67 which is 44.44
  The third session, the dog ate 1/3 of 44.44, leaving 2/3 of 44.44 which is 29.63
  The fourth session, the dog ate 1/3 of 29.63, leaving 2/3 of 29.63 which is 19.75
  Therefore, right before the dog began to eat at noon, the bowl was approximately 19.75% full.
  The answer is E: 40%.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Starting with the original amount, after the first hour, 2/3 of the food is left (1/3 is eaten). After the second hour, 2/3 * 2/3 = 4/9 of the food is left in the bowl (1/3 of 2/3 is eaten). After the third hour, 2/3 * 4/9 = 8/27 of the food is left in the bowl (1/3 of 4/9 is eaten). After the fourth hour, 2/3 * 8/27 = 16/81 of the food is left in the bowl (1/3 of 8/27 is eaten). So, right before the dog began to eat at noon, 16/81 of the original food is left in the bowl. We can convert this fraction to percent by multiplying by 100%.

  Therefore, the answer is (16/81) * 100 = 19.75 ≈ 20% (rounded to the nearest whole number).
  The answer is A: 20%.

  After the second feeding session (9 am), the amount of food remaining in the bowl would be (X - A) - A = X - 2A.

  Since the dog ate exactly once an hour, it consumed a total of (1/3) + (1/3) + (1/3) + (1/3) + (1/3) = 5/3 of the original food.
  Therefore, the amount of food remaining in the bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon is X - (5/3)X = (2/3)X.
  The percent of the original food in the bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon can be calculated as ((2/3)X / X) x 100 = 66.67%, which is approximately 67%.

  Therefore, the answer is E: 40%.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 28 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Anna is able to buy 5 more articles for $300 after the price of each article decreased by 15%. What is the new selling price of each article?
Choices:
  A: $8
  B: $10
  C: $13.6
  D: $22.9
  E: $40
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the original price of each article be x.
  A 15% decrease in the price of each article means its new selling price is 0.85x.
  If Anna can buy 5 more articles for $300, this means she originally had enough money to buy (300 / x) articles.
  After the price decreased, the number of articles she could buy with $300 increased by 5, which means that she was able to buy (300 / 0.85x) + 5 articles.
  These two expressions must be equal: (300 / x) = (300 / 0.85x) + 5
  Solving for x, we get x = 40. Therefore, the original selling price of each article was $40, and the new selling price is 0.85x = $34.
  The answer is not one of the choices listed. None of the above is the closest answer. 
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If Anna could buy 5 more articles for $300, then each article costs $60 ($300 divided by 5).
  The price of each article decreased by 15%, so the new price is 85% of the old price.
  We can set up an equation to solve for the new price: 85% * old price = new price.
  Plugging in the value of the old price, we get: 85% * $12 = $10.20.
  This means the new selling price of each article is $10.

Response 5:
Thought:
  If Anna can buy 5 more articles for $300 and the price of each article decreased by 15%, we can start forming an equation with the original number of articles and the original price of each article.
  Let x be the original price of each article.
  Let n be the original number of articles Anna could have bought with $300 at the original price x.
  We know that n(x - 15% of x) + 5(x - 15% of x) = 300
  We need to solve for x.
  Multiplying and simplifying, we have nx - 0.15nx + 5x - 0.75x = 300.
  Combining like terms, we have 0.85nx + 4.25x = 300.
  Solving for n, we get n = 300 / (0.85x + 4.25).
  We also know that the new price of each article will be x - 15% of x = 0.85x.
  Therefore, the new selling price of each article is 0.85x.
  We can now plug in the value of n to solve for x.
  However, this leads to an equation that is difficult to solve algebraically.
  We can use trial and error instead.
  Starting with choice A, if the original price of each article is $8, Anna can buy 37.5 articles at the original price or 42.5 articles (37.5 + 5) at the new price. 42.5 articles * $6.8 (0.85 * $8) is only $289, which is less than $300. Therefore, A is not the correct answer.
  Similarly, trying B, C, D, E, we find that only C, $13.6, satisfies the condition.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $13.6.

Question: In a survey of students, each student selected from a list of 10 songs the 2 songs that the student liked best. If each song was selected 5 times, how many students were surveyed?
Choices:
  A: 96
  B: 48
  C: 32
  D: 25
  E: 18
Response 0:
Thought:
  If each of the 10 songs was selected 5 times, then there were 50 selections made altogether.
  Since each student selected 2 songs they liked best, then there were 25 students surveyed.
  The answer is D: 25.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Each student selected 2 songs from the list of 10 songs, so there were a total of 20 song selections made by each student.
  Each song was selected 5 times.
  Therefore, there were 20 x 5 = 100 total song selections made by all students.
  Since each student made two selections, then the number of students who were surveyed is 100/2 = 50
  The answer is B: 48.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:

Action: Answer("D") 
Response 3:
Thought:
  Each student selects 2 songs from a list of 10 songs.
  Therefore, there are 10C2 or 45 ways to select 2 songs.
  But each song was selected 5 times.
  Therefore, the total number of selections made by the students is (5*10) = 50.
  Let the number of students surveyed be 'n'.
  Therefore, the total number of selections made by the students is equal to the total number of pairs of songs selected by the students which is nC2.
  We have nC2 = 50, solve to find n.
Calculation:
  nC2 = 50
  n!/[2!(n-2)!] = 50
  n(n-1)/2 = 50
  n(n-1) = 100
  n^2 - n - 100 = 0
  (n-10)(n+9) = 0
  n = 10 or n = -9
  Since the number of students surveyed cannot be negative, we choose n = 10.
  Therefore, 10 students were surveyed.

  Therefore, the number of students surveyed is 10 times some integer. Specifically, the number of students surveyed is 10*5 = 50.

Question: The original retail price of an appliance was 60 percent more than its wholesale cost. If the appliance was actually sold for 20 percent less than the original retail price, then it was sold for what percent more than its wholesale cost?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 28%
  C: 36%
  D: 40%
  E: 42%
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the Wholesale cost of the appliance = 100 (Assumption) then,
  
   The original retail price of an appliance = 100 + 60% of 100 = 100 + 60 = 160.
    
   20% less than the original retail price = 160 - 20% of 160 = 160 - 32 = 128.
   
   Difference in price = 128 - 100 = 28
   
   The percent increase from the wholesale price to the retail price = (28/100) * 100
   
   The answer is 28.
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let wholesale cost of the appliance be x.
  The original retail price of the appliance was 60% more than its wholesale cost, which means the original retail price = x + 0.6x = 1.6x.
  The appliance was actually sold for 20% less than the original retail price. Therefore, the selling price = (1 - 0.2) * 1.6x = 1.28x.
  The selling price is what percent more than its wholesale cost? Let's find out.
  Selling price is (1.28x/x) * 100% = 128% of the wholesale cost.
  Therefore, the appliance was sold for 28% more than its wholesale cost.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 32 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: When folded into two equal halves a rectangular sheet had a perimeter of 48cm for each part folded along one set of sides and the same is 66cm when folded along the other set of sides. Find the area of the sheet.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 1120
  C: 792
  D: 1320
  E: 1200
Response 0:
Thought:
Let l and b be the length and breadth of the rectangular sheet.
When folded along the length of the sheet, 2l + b = 48 cm
When folded along the breadth of the sheet, 2b + l = 66 cm
Solving these equations for l and b,
we get l = 42 cm and b = 6 cm
Area of the rectangular sheet = l * b = 42 * 6 = 252 sq.cm
When the sheet is folded, it becomes a rectangle half in size. So, the area of the folded sheet is (252 / 2) = 126 sq. cm.
Answer: Answer("A") 1584.
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's assume that the length and breadth of the rectangular sheet are l and b, respectively. When folded along one set of sides, the perimeter is 48 for each part, which means half-perimeter is 24. This indicates:
2(l+b) = 48
(l+b) = 24
Similarly, when folded along the other set of sides, the perimeter is 66 for each part, which means half-perimeter is 33. This indicates:
2(l+b) + 4w = 66
(l+b) + 2w = 33
Subtracting the first equation from the second equation gives:
2w = 9
w = 4.5
Now that we have the value of w, we can substitute it in either of the above equations to find the values of l and b.
(l+b) = 24
(l+4.5) = 24
l = 19.5
Therefore, the length and breadth of the rectangular sheet are 19.5 cm and 4.5 cm, respectively.
Area = l.b
Area = 19.5 * 4.5
Area = 87.75 cm²
Multiplying by 2 to account for both halves of the folded sheet, we get:
Area = 2 * 87.75
Area = 175.5 cm²
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Let's assume that the rectangular sheet is L units long and W units wide.
  When the sheet is folded in two equal halves along its length, we get a fold in the middle that is L/2 units long. The perimeter of each half is 48 cm, so:
     2L/2 + 2W = 48
     L + W = 24
  Similarly, when the sheet is folded in two equal halves along its width, we get a fold in the middle that is W/2 units long. The perimeter of each half is 66 cm, so:
     2W/2 + 2L = 66
     L + W = 33
  Now we have two equations with two unknowns (L and W). Solving for L and W, we get:
     L = 15
     W = 9
  Therefore, the area of the rectangular sheet is:
     A = L * W = 15 * 9 = 135 square cm
  The answer is not one of the choices.
  A possible mistake in the problem statement.

The second equation is L + 2B = 66 (when folded along the shorter side)
We can solve for 'L' and 'B' using these equations.
After finding 'L' and 'B', we can calculate the area of the sheet by multiplying 'L' and 'B'.

Thought:
  Let's say the length of the rectangle is L and the width is W.
  When folded along the length, we get two rectangles with lengths L/2 and width W. 
  The perimeter of the folded shape is 2(L/2 + W) = L+2W = 48. 
  Similarly, when folded along the width, we get two rectangles with lengths L and width W/2. 
  The perimeter of the folded shape is 2(L + W/2) = 2L + W = 66.
  We have two equations and two variables, which we can solve to find L and W.
  L + 2W = 48  ==> L = 48 - 2W.
  2L + W = 66  ==> substituting L from above, we get 2(48 - 2W) + W = 66
  ==> 96 -3W = 66  ==> 3W = 30  ==> W = 10, and L = 48 - 2W = 28.
  The area of the rectangle is L * W = 28 * 10 = 280cm^2.

Response 8:
Thought:
Let the length and breadth of the rectangular sheet be l and b, respectively.
When folded along one set of sides (lengthwise), the perimeter of each part is 48/2=24 cm.
When folded along the other set of sides (breadthwise), the perimeter of each part is 66/2=33 cm.
Perimeter of each part when folded along one set of sides = 2b + l = 24cm (eqn 1)
Perimeter of each part when folded along the other set of sides = 2l + b = 33cm (eqn 2)
Solving eqn 1 and 2 simultaneously to get l and b.
We get l=12cm and b=9cm.
Area of the rectangular sheet = lb = 12 × 9 = 108 sq cm = 10800 sq mm.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 9:
Thought:
  Let the length and width of the rectangle be L and W, respectively.
  Perimeter of the rectangle = 2(L+W)
  When folded along L, the perimeter of each part = 48/2 = 24 cm
  When folded along W, the perimeter of each part = 66/2 = 33 cm
  Perimeter of each part = 2(L/2 + W) or 2(L + W/2), respectively.
  Solving for L and W leads to two equations (L + W = 24 and 2L + W = 33), which can be solved simultaneously to find L and W.
  Once L and W are known, the area of the sheet can be calculated by multiplying the length and width.
  Therefore, A = LW

Question: On a normal day Bill usually averages about 15 mph when riding his bicycle. On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph. How far can Bill travel on a windy day in 21 minutes? Round to the nearest hundredth.
Choices:
  A: 2 miles
  B: 2.25 miles
  C: 3.25 miles
  D: 3.85 miles
  E: 2.85 miles

  Distance = speed x time.
  We need to convert the time into hours since the speed is given in mph.
  21 minutes is 21/60 = 0.35 hours.
  Therefore, the distance he can travel on a windy day is 11 x 0.35 = 3.85 miles.
  The answer is D: 3.85 miles.

Question: In a bag of red and green sweets, the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4. If the bag contains 120 green sweets, how many red sweets are there?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 80
  C: 95
  D: 100
  E: 85
Response 0:
Thought:
  The ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.
  This means that for every 3 red sweets, there are 4 green sweets.
  We are given the number of green sweets, which is 120.
  We can set up a proportion: 3/4 = x/120, where x is the number of red sweets.
  We can cross-multiply and solve for x.
  3/4 = x/120
  3 * 120 = 4 * x
  360 = 4x
  x = 90
  Therefore, there are 90 red sweets in the bag.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 35 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A number of friends decided to go on a picnic and planned to spend Rs. 96 on eatables. Four of them, however, did not turn up. As a consequence, the remaining ones had to contribute Rs. 4 extra, each. The number of those who attended the picnic was
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 12
  C: 16
  D: 24
  E: 25
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's assume that the cost of food was shared equally amongst all the friends who attended the picnic.
Let the number of people who attended the picnic be "x".
The cost of eatables per person is 96/x.
Since 4 people didn't turn up, the cost of eatables per person increased by 4 to become 96/(x-4) + 4 = 96/x.
On simplifying this equation, we get the quadratic equation: x^2 - 16x - 384 = 0.
The factors of -384 that add up to -16 are -24 and 16, so the number of friends who attended the picnic was 24.
Therefore, the answer is D: 24.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
- Let's take "x" as the number of friends who attended the picnic initially.
- The cost for each person if all attended = 96/x
- As four of them did not turn up, the cost has to be shared by (x-4) people.
- The cost now becomes 96/(x-4).
- It is given that each person has to contribute an additional Rs. 4 when 4 people didn't turn up.
- So, the new cost per person = (96/x) + 4. Also, (96/x) + 4 = 96/(x-4) since the cost of eatables remains the same in both the scenarios.
- Solving the equation we get, x = 12.
- Therefore, the answer is B: 12
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought: 
To solve the question, we need to use algebra.

Let "x" be the number of friends who attended the picnic.
Since the 4 friends didn't show up, "x-4" friends had to contribute extra Rs. 4 each.
Therefore, the total amount of money collected would still be Rs. 96, So:

    x*(96/x) = (x-4)*(96/x + 4)

Simplifying the above equation, we get:

    x^2 - 32x - 192 = 0

Factoring this quadratic expression, we get:

    (x-24)*(x+8) = 0

Hence, the possible values for "x" are x = 24 (which is a positive integer).

So the answer is D: 24.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Thought:
Let's start by assuming that the total number of friends who were supposed to turn up is 'x'.
Then, the total cost would be distributed among 'x' friends.
Since 4 of them didn't turn up, the cost is now distributed among 'x-4' friends.
Each of these 'x-4' have to contribute an additional Rs.4
Using this information, we can create an equation:
  96 = (x-4)*c + 4(x-4)
  where 'c' is the amount each person was supposed to contribute.
Simplifying this equation:
  96 = cx - 4c + 4x - 16
  96 = (c+4)x - 4c - 16
  112 = (c+4)x - 4c
  28 = (c+1)x - c
Now we have two equations:
  cx = 96 (from the total cost equation)
  28 = (c+1)x - c
  28 = cx + x 
  28 = 96 + x
  x = 28 - 96 = -68 (which does not make sense since x is the number of attendees)

Since 'x' represents the number of friends who were supposed to turn up, we need to find the number of friends who actually attended the picnic. Let's assume that 'y' friends attended. 
Then, we can create another equation using the given information: 
  y*c = 96
We know that each of the 'y' friends had to contribute an extra Rs.4.
So, the cost is now distributed among 'y' friends, and each of them has to contribute 'c+4'.
We can create another equation:
  (y*c) + 4*(y-4) = 96
  y*c -16 = 96
  y*c = 112
  y = 112/c
  
Using these equations, we can solve for 'y':
  y = 112/c
  y*c = 96
  c = 96/y
  Substitute c in equation 1: y*c = 112
  y(96/y) = 112
  96 = 112/y
  y = 112/96
  y = 1.17 (which does not make sense since y represents the number of attendees)
  
The closest integer to 112/96 is 1. Therefore, 'y' is equal to 1.
That means only 1 friend attended the picnic.

Total estimated cost / n = Total actual cost / (n-4) + 4

Calculation:
  Total estimated cost: Rs. 96
  Let's assume the number of people initially planned to participate is n.
  Hence, each person was supposed to pay Rs. 96/n.
  
  Total actual cost: Rs. 96 - 4*4 = Rs. 80
  Each person actually paid Rs. 96/n + 4.
  
  Therefore, Rs. 96/n + 4 = 80/(n-4) + 4

  Solving the above quadratic equation, we get n = 16 (after rejecting the negative solution)

Therefore, 16 people attended the picnic.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 37 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: there are more than 501 students in a school such that 20% of them exactly took physics and 28% of them exactly took math. What could be the least possible no of students in the school?
Choices:
  A: 550
  B: 570
  C: 600
  D: 700
  E: none of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the number of students in the school is "x".
  According to the problem, 20% of the x number of students took physics, which is 0.2x students.
  Also, 28% of the x number of students took math, which is 0.28x students.
  Hence, the total number of students taking either physics or math is 0.2x + 0.28x = 0.48x.
  According to the problem, this number is greater than 501.
  Therefore, 0.48x > 501
  Solving the equation, x > 1043.75
  Since x is greater than 1043.75 and has to be an integer, the least possible value for x is 1044.
  The answer is C: 600.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
To find the minimum number of students, we want to assume that the smallest percentage of students possible took physics and math. 
We know that 20% of students took physics, and 28% took math. If some students took both, then that means the total percentage of students who took at least one of the classes is more than 20% + 28%, which is 48%.
If we assume that no students took both classes, then the minimum percentage of students who took at least one of the classes is 20% + 28% - 100% = 48%. Therefore, we know that 52% of students didn't take either class.
We want to find the minimum number of students, so we want to maximize the percentage of students who didn't take either class. To do this, we want to assume that as many students as possible took both classes. If all of the students who took physics also took math, then the percentage of students who didn't take either class is 100% - 20% - (28% - 20%) = 52%. So, we want to find the minimum number of students such that 52% of them is greater than 501.
(52/100)*n = 501
n ≥ 963.46

Question: Two cars are travelling from the same starting point in the same direction, having started their commute at the same time. The first car travels at a steady rate of 55 mph, while the second travels at a steady rate of 52 mph. How much time will pass before the cars are 15 miles away from each other?
Choices:
  A: 3 hours
  B: 5 hours
  C: 6 hours
  D: 4 hours
  E: 7 hours
Response 0:
Thought:
  The first car is moving at a speed of 55 mph, while the second car is moving at a speed of 52 mph.
  Hence, the relative speed between the two cars is 3 mph.
  We need to find the time when the distance between the two cars is 15 miles.
  The formula for calculating the time is time = distance / relative speed.
  Plugging in the given values, we get time = 15 / 3 = 5 hours.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 5 hours.

Question: A man wants to eat fruit for breakfast and vegetable for dinner. He has 6 different types of fruit and 8 different types of vegetables. He can only eat one type at a time. In how many ways can he eat breakfast and dinner.
Choices:
  A: 54
  B: 24
  C: 48
  D: 20
  E: 36
Response 0:
Thought:
  The man has 6 options for breakfast.
  He has 8 options for dinner.
  Each meal choice is independent of the other.
  Therefore, the total number of ways he can eat breakfast and dinner is the product of the number of ways he can choose each meal.
  The answer is 6 x 8 = 48.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:

  The number of ways he can eat fruit for breakfast is 6.
  The number of ways he can eat vegetable for dinner is 8.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 40 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Suppose for any real number x, [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x. Let L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] and R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]. Then it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which
Choices:
  A: L(x,y) = R(x,y)
  B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y)
  C: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
  D: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought:
We need to find the relation between L(x,y) and R(x,y) and check which of the given choices is correct.
L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y]
R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]
For simplicity, we can assume that x = a + b and y = c + d where a,b,c,d are positive integers and 0 ≤ b < 1 and 0 ≤ d < 1. 
Thus, [x] = a and [y] = c and [x+y] = a + c if a + c < 1 and a + c + 1 if a + c ≥ 1
Also, [2x] = 2a if b < 0.5 and [2x] = 2a + 1 if b ≥ 0.5
Similarly, [2y] = 2c if d < 0.5 and [2y] = 2c + 1 if d ≥ 0.5.
Now, we can substitute these values into the expressions to compare:
L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] = a + c + [a + b + c + d]
R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y] = 2a + 2c
Thus, if a + c < 0.5, then [a+b+c+d] = 0 and L(x,y) = 2a + 2c
If 0.5 ≤ a + c < 1, then [a+b+c+d] = 1 and L(x,y) = 2a + 2c + 1
If a + c ≥ 1, then [a+b+c+d] = 2 and L(x,y) = 2a + 2c + 2
Thus, L(x,y) can only take on three possible values: 2a + 2c, 2a + 2c + 1, 2a + 2c + 2.
On the other hand, R(x,y) can only take on two possible values: 2a + 2c, 2a + 2c + 2.
Now, we can compare L(x,y) and R(x,y) to check which of the given choices is correct.
A: L(x,y) = R(x,y) is possible if a + c + 1 = 2a + 2c or a + c = 1, which is possible when a = 0 and c = 1 or a = 1 and c = 0.
B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y) is true since L(x,y) can take on three possible values and R(x,y) can take on two possible values.
C: L(x,y) < R(x,y) is possible if a + c < 0.5, which is possible if a = 0 and c = 0.
D: L(x,y) > R(x,y) is possible if a + c ≥ 1, which is possible if a = 1 and c = 1.
E: None of the above is not correct since B is a correct option.
Therefore, the answer is B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y).
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's start by rewriting the function using the greatest integer function formula:
  [x] = the largest integer n such that n is less than or equal to x.
  [y] = the largest integer m such that m is less than or equal to y.
  [x + y] = the largest integer p such that p is less than or equal to x+y.
  [2x] = the largest integer q such that q is less than or equal to 2x.
  [2y] = the largest integer r such that r is less than or equal to 2y.

  L(x, y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y]
          = n + m + p where n, m, and p are integers

  R(x, y) = [2x] + [2y]
          = q + r where q and r are integers
          
  Since L(x,y) = n + m + p and R(x,y) = q + r, it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which
  A: L(x,y) = R(x,y)
     If we take x = y = 1, then L(x,y) = [1] + [1] + [1+1] = 1+1+2=4,
     but R(x,y) = [2(1)] + [2(1)] = 2+2=4, which contradicts the statement.
  
  By observing that [x+y] is less than or equal to x+y and [2x] is greater than or equal to 2x, we can conclude that:
  B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y) 
     It is always true since the left-hand side counts x and y three times, while the right-hand side counts x and y twice.

  C: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
     We can prove that by using x=0.4,y=0.3 as an example.
     L(x,y) = [0] + [0] + [0.7] = 0 + 0 + 0 = 0
     R(x,y) = [2(0.4)] + [2(0.3)] = [0.8] + [0.6] = 0 + 0 = 0
     Clearly, L(x,y) is less than R(x,y). 
    
  D: L(x,y) > R(x,y)
     It is impossible that L(x,y) is greater than R(x,y) since L(x,y) can be at most equal to R(x,y) due to the observation earlier.

  Therefore, the answer is C: L(x,y) < R(x,y).

    [x] means the greatest integer less than or equal to x.
    [y] means the greatest integer less than or equal to y.
    [x+y] means the greatest integer less than or equal to the sum of x and y.
    [2x] means the greatest integer less than or equal to 2x.
    [2y] means the greatest integer less than or equal to 2y.
    Therefore, [x], [y], and [x+y] are always integers, whereas [2x] and [2y] may or may not be integers.
    We can use the inequality 2x - 1 < [2x] ≤ 2x to show that [2x] = 2x - 1 if and only if x is not an integer.
    Similarly, we can use the inequality 2y - 1 < [2y] ≤ 2y to show that [2y] = 2y - 1 if and only if y is not an integer.
    Now, suppose L(x,y) = R(x,y). Then [x] + [y] + [x + y] = [2x] + [2y], which implies that [x+y] is an even integer.
    But [x+y] can also be written as [2(x+y)/2] = [2x+2y]/2, which implies that [2x+2y] is an even integer.    
    This means that (2x+2y) - 2 < [2x+2y] ≤ (2x+2y), which implies that [2x] + [2y] = 2x + 2y - 2.

    Hence, it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which L(x,y) = R(x,y).
    The answer is A: L(x,y) = R(x,y).

  A: L(x,y) = R(x,y)

  B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y)

  C: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
  If x and y are positive, then L(x,y) cannot be greater than R(x,y) since the greatest integer function always rounds down. Therefore, this option is impossible.
  D: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
  This option is the same as C, so it is not possible.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 41 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: While selling a watch, a shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%. If he gives a discount of 7%, he earns Rs. 15 less as profit. The marked price of the watch is:
Choices:
  A: Rs. 697.50
  B: Rs. 712.50
  C: Rs. 787.50
  D: Rs. 750
  E: Rs. 780
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's assume that the marked price of the watch is MP.
With a discount of 5%, the selling price is MP - 0.05MP = 0.95MP.
With a discount of 7%, the selling price is MP - 0.07MP = 0.93MP.
If the shopkeeper earns a profit of P with a discount of 5%, then his profit with a discount of 7% is (P - 15).
Therefore, 0.95MP - P = 0.93MP - (P - 15).
By solving this equation, we get P = 375.
So, the cost price of the watch for the shopkeeper is CP = MP - P = 0.95MP - 375.
We need to determine MP from the given choices. 
Let's put each choice in the expression of CP = 0.95MP - 375 and check which satisfies the equation. 
  - For A: CP = (0.95 × 697.50) - 375 = Rs. 301.625, which is incorrect as the cost price can't be negative.
  - For B: CP = (0.95 × 712.50) - 375 = Rs. 306.875, which is incorrect as the cost price can't be negative.
  - For C: CP = (0.95 × 787.50) - 375 = Rs. 369.125, which is correct as this is the cost price if MP is Rs. 787.50.
  - For D: CP = (0.95 × 750) - 375 = Rs. 281.25, which is incorrect as the cost price can't be negative.
  - For E: CP = (0.95 × 780) - 375 = Rs. 328.50, which is incorrect as the cost price can't be negative.
The marked price of the watch is Rs. 787.50.
Therefore, the answer is C: Rs. 787.50. 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let the marked price of the watch be M.
Then, selling price of watch after 5% discount = M - 0.05M = 0.95M
Selling price of watch after 7% discount = M - 0.07M = 0.93M
Given, the shopkeeper earns Rs. 15 less with 7% discount as compared to 5% discount.
So, 0.95M - 0.93M = 15
0.02M = 15
M = 15/0.02
M = 750
Therefore, the marked price of the watch is Rs. 750.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 43 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is:
Choices:
  A: 2.6m
  B: 3.9m
  C: 4m
  D: 4.2m
  E: 4.4m
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let the height of the room be "2x".
  Let the semi-perimeter of the room be "5y".
  The perimeter of the room is "10y".
  The length of each wall is equal to the height of the room which is "2x".
  The total area of the four walls is equal to the semi-perimeter multiplied by the height which is "5y * 2x = 10xy".
  The area of doors and windows is given to be 15 sq.m.
  The area of the four walls is equal to the area of the doors and windows plus the area to be papered.
  The area to be papered is equal to the area of the four walls minus the area of the doors and windows which is "(10xy - 15) sq.m".
  The area to be papered is equal to the cost of the paper multiplied by the length of the paper which is "260 = 2 * 0.5 * (10xy - 15) = xy - 15/4".
  Solving for xy, we get "xy = 265/4".
  Substituting "xy = 265/4" in "2x/5y = 2/5", we get "x/y = 1/5".
  Solving for x and y, we get "x = 2" and "y = 10".
  Therefore, the height of the room is "2x = 4".
  The answer is C: 4m.
Action: Answer("C")

Thought:

  Then, 2x/5y = 2/5 => x/y = 1.

  Then, 2x + L + B = 5y.
  Also, (L/2 + B/2) x 2 + 15 = area of the four walls in sq.m.
  => L+B+30 = 200.
  => L+B = 170.
  And, 2x + 170 = 5y.

  => 4x + 340 = 10y.

  => x = 5.85.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 44 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man walks at 5 kmph for 6 hrs and at 4 kmph for 12 hrs. His average speed is
Choices:
  A: 4 1/3 km/h
  B: 7 2/3 km/h
  C: 9 ½ km/h
  D: 8 km/h
  E: 81 km/h
Response 0:
Thought:
  Average Speed = Total Distance / Total Time
  Distance = Speed x Time
  Let's calculate the total distance first
  Distance covered at 5 kmph for 6 hrs = 5 x 6 = 30 km
  Distance covered at 4 kmph for 12 hrs = 4 x 12 = 48 km
  Total distance covered = 30 + 48 = 78 km
  Total Time taken = 6 + 12 = 18 hrs
  Average Speed = 78 / 18 = 13/3 kmph
  In mixed fraction, 13/3 = 4 1/3 km/h
  Therefore, the answer is A: 4 1/3 km/h
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Average speed is the total distance covered by the total time taken.
  Let's calculate the total distance first.
  Distance traveled in the first 6 hours = 5 kmph * 6 hours = 30 km
  Distance traveled in the next 12 hours = 4 kmph * 12 hours = 48 km
  Total distance traveled = 30 km + 48 km = 78 km
  Total time taken = 6 hours + 12 hours = 18 hours
  Therefore, the average speed is (Total distance traveled) / (Total time taken) = (78 km) / (18 hours) = 4 1/3 km/h
  The answer is A: 4 1/3 km/h.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 46 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The difference between the squares of two numbers is 256000 and the sum of the numbers is 1000. The numbers are
Choices:
  A: 600, 400
  B: 628, 372
  C: 640, 360
  D: None of these
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's assume that the two numbers are x and y.
  We know that the difference between the squares of the two numbers is 256000.
  Therefore, we can set up the equation: x^2 - y^2 = 256000.
  This equation can be factored into (x+y)(x-y) = 256000.
  We also know that the sum of the two numbers is 1000.
  Therefore, we can set up another equation: x+y=1000
  Now we have two equations and two variables and we can solve them simultaneously.
  We can use the second equation to substitute (x+y) in the first equation: (x+y)(x-y) = 256000. 
  (1000)(x-y) = 256000.
  x-y = 256.
  We have two equations and two variables, we can solve them using any method to get the answer.
  By solving them simultaneously, we get x=628 and y=372.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 628, 372.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's suppose the numbers are x and y. Therefore, we have two equations:
  x + y = 1000    (Equation 1)
  x^2 - y^2 = 256000   (Equation 2)
  
We can use Equation 1 to isolate y:
  y = 1000 - x
  
Substitute this value of y into Equation 2:
  x^2 - (1000 - x)^2 = 256000
  
Simplifying:
  x^2 - (1000^2 - 2000x + x^2) = 256000
  -1000^2 + 2000x = 256000
  2000x = 256000+1000000
  x = 628
  
Substitute this value of x back into Equation 1 to find y:
  y = 1000 - x = 372
  
Therefore, the numbers are 628 and 372, which corresponds to choice B.

  x + y = 1000    ...(2)

  x^2 - (1000-x)^2 = 256000
  x^2 - (1000000 - 2000x + x^2) = 256000
  2x^2 - 2000x + 744000 = 0

  1000(x - y) = 256000

  We now have two equations with two variables; we can use one of several methods to solve the system of equations to find x and y.

  x = 1000 - y

  2y = 744
  y = 372
  
  We can substitute this value of y back into the equation x + y = 1000 to find x:
  x + 372 = 1000
  x = 628
  
  Therefore, the numbers are 628 and 372.
  The answer is B: 628, 372.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 9:
Thought: 
  We know that the difference between the squares of two numbers is 256000.
  Let's assume that the two numbers are x and y, where x > y.
  We can set up two equations:
    x^2 - y^2 = 256000   (equation 1)
    x + y = 1000         (equation 2)
  We can factor equation 1 as (x+y)(x-y) = 256000.
  Since x+y = 1000, we can write equation 1 as 1000(x-y) = 256000.
  Solving for x-y, we get x-y = 256.
  Adding equations 1 and 2, we get 2x = 1256.
  Therefore, x = 628, and y = 372.
  The answer is B: 628, 372.

Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ?
Choices:
  A: 226
  B: 230
  C: 240
  D: 260
  E: 280
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The yearly profit (P) is equal to the revenue from sales minus the production costs.
  The total revenue from sales is equal to the number of units (n) produced multiplied by the selling price per unit (s).
  n = 420 components/month x 12 months/year = 5040 components/year
  To calculate the minimum selling price per component that will generate a profit of at least $626,400, we can use the following equation:
  P = n(s - 110) >= 626400
  s >= (626400 + n(110)) / n
  s >= (626400 + 5040(110)) / 5040
  s >= $230 per component
  Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee a yearly profit of at least $626,400 is $230.
  The answer is B: 230.

Question: If m > 0, y > 0, and x is m percent of 4y, then, in terms of y, m is what percentage of x?
Choices:
  A: y/400
  B: 4y
  C: 50y
  D: 2500/y
  E: 5000/y
Response 0:
Thought:
  If x is m percent of 4y, then we can write it as x = (m/100)*4y = 4my/100.
  We want to find m as a percentage of x in terms of y.
  m as a percentage of x is (m/x)*100.
  Substituting x = 4my/100, we get (m/(4my/100))*100 = 25/y.
  Therefore, m as a percentage of x in terms of y is 25/y.
  The answer is not one of the given choices.
  The closest answer is D: 2500/y.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:

  Solving for m in the equation x = 4my/100, we get m = 25x/y.

  m/x = (25x/y)/x = 25/y * 1/x.
  To convert this to a percentage, we need to multiply by 100, which gives us 2500/yx.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 2500/y.
