### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Thought:
- If each employee contributed Rs. "x", and there are "n" employees, the total contribution will be "n * x"
- We have two equations: 
    1. n*x = 6,00,000
    2. n * (x+60) = 6,24,000
- Divide equation-2 by equation-1, we get (n(x+60))/(nx) = 6,24,000/6,00,000
- Simplifying the above equation we get x = 600. 
- Substituting value of x in equation-1, we get n = 1000.
- The number of employees is 1000.
- The answer is D: 100.
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
First, let's consider the contribution of each employee as 'x'. 
If the total contribution of the employees is 'y', then according to the question;
  x * n = y --- (1)
where 'n' is the number of employees.
Also, if each employee would have contributed Rs. 60 extra, then the total contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh, which can be written as;
  (x+60) * n = 624000 --- (2)
Now, we can solve equations (1) and (2) simultaneously to get the value of 'n'.
  x * n = y => x = y/n
  (x+60) * n = 624000
  => x*n + 60n = 624000
  => (y/n)*n + 60n = 624000
  => y + 60n^2 = 624000n
  => 600000 = n(y/n + 60n)
  => 600000 = y + 60n^2          [as y/n = x => y = nx]
  => 600000 = nx + 60n^2
  => 600000 = n(x + 60n)
  => n = 600000/(x + 60n)

Now, substituting the given values in the above equation to get the value of 'n'.
  n = 600000/(x + 60n)
  => n = 600000/(6,00,000/ n + 60n)
  => n = 100

Therefore, there are 100 employees in that organization.
The answer is D: 100.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let's assume there are 'n' employees and the amount that each employee should contribute is 'x'
  The total amount raised by n employees without the additional contribution is 6 lakh i.e. n * x = 600000
  The total amount raised by n employees with the additional contribution is 6.24 lakh i.e. n * (x + 60) = 624000
  Solving these two equations, we can find the value of 'n'
  n * x = 600000  --> x = 600000/n
  n * (x + 60) = 624000
  Substituting the value of x in this equation, we get:
  n * (600000/n + 60) = 624000
  660000 + 60n = 624000n/n
  660000n = 624000n - 60n^2
  60n^2 = 36000n
  n = 600
  Therefore, there are 600 employees in the organization.
  The answer is not one of the available choices.
  Therefore, the answer is "None of the Above".
  
Note: Rounding off the answer to the nearest integer can give us an answer close to one of the given choices.

  Substituting y in the second equation, we get (100 * (6000 + 60)) = 6,24,000.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 100.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Thought:
Let the amount each nephew receive be Rs. x.
Then, each daughter will receive 4x and each son will receive 5x.
The total number of people who receive the money is 5+4+2 = 11.
The total amount divided among them is Rs. 8600.
So, (5x * 5) + (4x * 4) + (2x * 2) = 8600
Simplifying the equation, we get, 45x = 8600
Therefore, x = 8600/45 = 191.11
So, each nephew receives Rs. 191.11, each daughter receives 4x = 4 * 191.11 = 764.44
The answer is Rs. 764.44 which is closest to option C: Rs. 600.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let the share of each nephew = x
The share of one daughter = 4x
The share of one son = 5x

Total number of family members = 5 sons + 4 daughters + 2 nephews = 11
Total amount = Rs. 8600

The total number of shares = 5 + 4 + 2 = 11
5x + 4(4x) + 2x = 8600
Simplifying the equation, we get
21x = 8600
x = Rs. 400

One daughter share = 4x = 4 * 400 = Rs. 1600

Therefore, each daughter receives Rs. 1600.

Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's consider the number to be x.
  The student found the value of 7/18 of the number i.e., (7/18)*x.
  Actual value of 7/8 of the number i.e., (7/8)*x.
  The difference between the actual value and student's answer is 770.
  So, (7/8)*x - (7/18)*x = 770.
  Solving this equation gives us x = 1584.
  Therefore, the number is 1584.
  The answer is A: 1584.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's suppose the actual number is 'x'.
The student intended to find (7/8)x, but instead found (7/18)x.
So, the difference is ((7/8) - (7/18))x = (49/72)x.
We know that this difference is equal to 770.
Thus, (49/72)x = 770.
Now, we can solve the equation for 'x' by multiplying both sides by (72/49).
So x = (72/49) * 770=  1120.
Therefore, the answer is D: 1656.

Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Thought process:
  - For every ride, the cab will charge $3.50 for the first quarter mile.
  - We will be left with $8.50-$3.50 = $5 for the remaining distance.
  - For the remaining distance, the cab charges 10 cents/quarter mile, or equivalently $0.10/0.25 miles = $0.40 per mile.
  - So, we can travel $5/$0.40 = 12.5 miles by the remaining amount.
  - However, we have already travelled a quarter mile in the beginning, so the maximum distance we can travel is 12.5 + 0.25 = 12.75 miles.
Calculation: 
  The maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab is 12.75 miles.
Answer: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  For the first quarter-mile, the cost is $3.50, which uses up $3.50.
  The remaining amount that we can spend on additional quarter miles is $8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00
  Each additional quarter-mile costs $0.10.
  So to find out how many quarter-miles we can go, we divide $5.00 by $0.10: $5.00 / $0.10 = 50 quarter-miles.
  Therefore, the total distance we can travel is 0.25 (for the first quarter-mile) + 50 × 0.25 = 13 miles.
  However, the question is asking for the maximum distance we can travel, which occurs when we pay exactly $8.50.
  If we divide $8.50 by the cost per quarter-mile, we get $8.50 / $0.10 = 85 quarter-miles.
  Therefore, the maximum distance we can travel is 0.25 (for the first quarter-mile) + 85 × 0.25 = 21.5 miles. 
  However, this calculation assumes that the cab driver will take us exactly 85 quarter-miles, which is unlikely.
  Therefore, we should round down to the nearest quarter-mile to get a more realistic answer.

Response 2:
Thought:
To find the maximum distance, I need to divide the total money I have by the cost per quarter mile. But the cost per quarter mile is not constant, it has a fixed cost of $3.50 for the first quarter mile, and then it's 10 cents per additional quarter mile. So, I need to use two different formulas to calculate the total cost and then determine the maximum distance. 

Calculation:
First, I calculate how many quarter miles I can travel by subtracting the fixed cost from the total money and then dividing the result by the variable cost.

$8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00
$5.00 ÷ $0.10 = 50 quarter miles

But I traveled one quarter mile already, so I need to subtract it from the total and then convert the remaining quarter miles to miles:

50 - 1 = 49
49 × 0.25 = 12.25 miles

Therefore, the maximum distance I can travel is 12.25 miles, which is closest to choice B: 12.75 miles.

Response 3:
Thought:
To solve the problem, I need to find how many quarter-miles can be covered for $5 then add the distance for the remaining $3.50.
  The cost of the first quarter-mile is $3.50.
  The cost of each additional quarter-mile is $0.10.
  To cover $5, the number of additional quarter-miles covered is (500 - 350) / 10 = 15.
  Therefore, the total distance covered is 1 + 15 = 16 quarter-miles.
  Each quarter-mile is 0.25 miles, so the total distance covered is 16 x 0.25 = 4 miles.
  The remaining $3.50 can cover an additional 3.50 / 0.10 = 35 additional quarter-miles.
  The total distance covered is 4 + (35 x 0.25) = 4 + 8.75 = 12.75 miles.
  The answer is B: 12.75 miles.

  First, figure out how much distance can be covered with $5.
  One mile is equal to 4 quarter-miles. Therefore, the cab fare for 1 mile is:
    $3.50 for the first quarter-mile + 3 * $0.10 for the remaining 3 quarter-miles = $3.80
  The cost of a mile is $3.80.
  With $5, the distance that can be traveled is:
    $5 ÷ $3.80 per mile = 1.3157 miles
    Since 1 mile = 4 quarter-miles, 
    The remaining distance that can be covered is:  1.3157 x 4 = 5.26 quarter miles
  The total distance that can be covered is:
    0.25 miles (for the initial $3.50) + 5.26 quarter miles (for the remaining $5) = 1.315 miles + 5.26 quarter miles = 3.765 miles
  Therefore, the maximum distance that can be traveled with $8.50 is 3.765 miles.

Response 6:
Thought:
To calculate the maximum distance, we need to find out how many quarter-miles we can travel with the $5.50.
The first quarter-mile costs $3.50. So, we have left with $8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00.
Each additional quarter-mile costs ten cents or $0.10.
Therefore, we can travel the remaining [($5.00) / ($0.10/quarter-mile)] = 50 quarter-miles.
The total distance is the sum of the first quarter-mile and the additional 50 quarter-miles.
So, the total distance we can travel is [1 + 50] / 4 = 12.75 miles.
Therefore, the answer is B: 12.75 miles.

Response 7:
Thought:
To determine the maximum distance, we will divide the cost of the ride by the cost per quarter-mile. 

Formula:
Let d be the maximum distance.
Initial charge is $3.50
Additional cost is ($8.50 - $3.50) = $5.00
Each quarter mile costs $0.10, which is equivalent to 25 cents per one mile. 

We can set up the following equation:
$5.00 = $0.25d

Solving for d:
d = $5.00 / $0.25
d = 20

Therefore, the maximum distance that can be traveled is 20 quarter miles or 5 miles.

- We can find the number of miles we can travel before the cost exceeds $8.50 by subtracting the initial fare from $8.50 and then dividing the result by the cost per mile.
- The initial fare is $3.50, so we have $8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00 to spend on additional miles.
- The cost per mile is $0.40, so we can travel $5.00 ÷ $0.40/mile = 12.5 miles before the cost exceeds $8.50.
- However, we need to convert this distance into quarter-miles, because the fare is charged in quarter-mile increments.
- There are 4 quarter-miles in a mile, so we have 12.5 miles x 4 quarter-miles/mile = 50 quarter-miles.
- We have already traveled the first quarter-mile, so we need to subtract that from the total: 50 quarter-miles - 1 quarter-mile = 49 quarter-miles.
- Therefore, we can travel 49 quarter-miles on $8.50.
